If the cookiejar has recorded the next timestamp at which one or\\n379:  * more cookies expire, then processing will exit early in case this timestamp\\n380:  * is in the future.\\n381:  */\\n382: static void remove_expired(struct CookieInfo *cookies)\\n383: {\\n384:   struct Cookie *co, *nx;\\n385:   curl_off_t now = (curl_off_t)time(NULL);\\n386:   unsigned int i;\\n387: \\n388:   /*\\n389:    * If the earliest expiration timestamp in the jar is in the future we can\\n390:    * skip scanning the whole jar and instead exit early as there won't be any\\n391:    * cookies to evict. If the cookiejar has recorded the next timestamp at which one or\n379:  * more cookies expire, then processing will exit early in case this timestamp\n380:  * is in the future.\n381:  */\n382: static void remove_expired(struct CookieInfo *cookies)\n383: {\n384:   struct Cookie *co, *nx;\n385:   curl_off_t now = (curl_off_t)time(NULL);\n386:   unsigned int i;\n387: \n388:   /*\n389:    * If the earliest expiration timestamp in the jar is in the future we can\n390:    * skip scanning the whole jar and instead exit early as there won't be any\n391:    * cookies to evict. While the name says read, this function both reads\n601:          * and writes away the data. The returned 'nread' holds the number\n602:          * of actual data it wrote to the client.\n603:          */\n604:         CURLcode extra;\n605:         CHUNKcode res =\n606:           Curl_httpchunk_read(data, k->str, nread, &nread, &extra);\n607: \n608:         if(CHUNKE_OK < res) {\n609:           if(CHUNKE_PASSTHRU_ERROR == res) {\n610:             failf(data, \"Failed reading the chunked-encoded stream\");\n611:             result = extra;\n612:             goto out;\n613:           }\n614:           failf(data, \"%s in chunked-encoding\", Curl_chunked_strerror(res));\n615:           result = CURLE_RECV_ERROR;\n616:           goto out;\n617:         }\n618:         if(CHUNKE_STOP == res) {\n619:           /* we're done reading chunks! It should keep reading. */\n664:         if(!is_http3) {\n665:           k->keepon &= ~KEEP_RECV; /* we're done reading */\n666:         }\n667:       }\n668: \n669:       k->bytecount += nread;\n670:       max_recv -= nread;\n671: \n672:       result = Curl_pgrsSetDownloadCounter(data, k->bytecount);\n673:       if(result)\n674:         goto out;\n675: \n676:       if(!k->chunk && (nread || k->badheader || is_empty_data)) {\n677:         /* If this is chunky transfer, it was already written */\n678: \n679:         if(k->badheader && !k->ignorebody) {\n680:           /* we parsed a piece of data wrongly assuming it was a header\n681:              and now we output it as body instead */\n682:           size_t headlen = Curl_dyn_len(&data->state.headerb);\n683: \n684:           /* Don't let excess data pollute body writes */\n685:           if(k->maxdownload == -1 || (curl_off_t)headlen <= k->maxdownload)\n686:             result = Curl_client_write(data, CLIENTWRITE_BODY,\n687:                                        Curl_dyn_ptr(&data->state.headerb),\n688:                                        headlen);\n689:           else\n690:             result = Curl_client_write(data, CLIENTWRITE_BODY,\n691:                                        Curl_dyn_ptr(&data->state.headerb),\n692:                                        (size_t)k->maxdownload);\n693: \n694:           if(result)\n695:             goto out;\n696:         }\n697:         if(k->badheader < HEADER_ALLBAD) {\n698:           /* This switch handles various content encodings.              \" milliseconds with %\" CURL_FORMAT_CURL_OFF_T \" bytes received\",\n1201:               Curl_timediff(now, data->progress.t_startsingle),\n1202:               k->bytecount);\n1203:       }\n1204:       result = CURLE_OPERATION_TIMEDOUT;\n1205:       goto out;\n1206:     }\n1207:   }\n1208:   else {\n1209:     /*\n1210:      * The transfer has been performed. Just make some general checks before\n1211:      * returning.\n1212:      */\n1213: \n1214:     if(!(data->req.no_body) && (k->size != -1) &&\n1215:        (k->bytecount != k->size) &&\n1216: #ifdef CURL_DO_LINEEND_CONV\n1217:        /* Most FTP servers don't adjust their file SIZE response for CRLFs,\n1218:           so we'll check to see if the discrepancy can be explained\n1219:           by the number of CRLFs we've changed to LFs.\n1220:        */\n1221:        (k->bytecount != (k->size + data->state.crlf_conversions)) &&\n1222: #endif /* CURL_DO_LINEEND_CONV */\n1223:        !k->newurl) {\n1224:       failf(data, \"transfer closed with %\" CURL_FORMAT_CURL_OFF_T\n1225:             \" bytes remaining to read\", k->size - k->bytecount);\n1226:       result = CURLE_PARTIAL_FILE;\n1227:       goto out;\n1228:     }\n1229:     if(!(data->req.no_body) && k->chunk &&\n1230:        (conn->chunk.state != CHUNK_STOP)) {\n1231:       /*\n1232:        * In chunked mode, return an error if the connection is closed prior to\n1233:        * the empty (terminating) chunk is read.\n1234:        *\n1235:        * The condition above used to check for\n1236:        * conn->proto.http->chunk.datasize != 0 which is true after reading\n1237:        * *any* chunk, not just the empty chunk.\n1238:        *\n1239:        */\n1240:       failf(data, \"transfer closed with outstanding read data remaining\");\n1241:       result = CURLE_PARTIAL_FILE;\n1242:       goto out;\n1243:     }\n1244:     if(Curl_pgrsUpdate(data)) {\n1245:       result = CURLE_ABORTED_BY_CALLBACK;\n1246:       goto out;\n1247:     }\n1248:   }\n1249: \n1250:   /* Now update the \"done\" boolean we return */\n1251:   *done = (0 == (k->keepon&(KEEP_RECVBITS|KEEP_SENDBITS))) ? TRUE : FALSE;\n1252: out:\n1253:   if(result)\n1254:     DEBUGF(infof(data, \"Curl_readwrite() -> %d\", result));\n1255:   return result;\n1256: }\n1257: \n1258: /*\n1259:  * Curl_single_getsock() gets called by the multi interface code when the app\n1260:  * has requested to get the sockets for the current connection. This function\n1261:  * will then be called once for every connection that the multi interface\n1262:  * keeps track of. This function will only be called for connections that are\n1263:  * in the proper state to have this information available.\n1264:  */\n1265: int Curl_single_getsock(struct Curl_easy *data,\n1266:                         struct connectdata *conn,\n1267:                         curl_socket_t *sock)\n1268: {\n1269:   int bitmap = GETSOCK_BLANK;\n1270:   unsigned sockindex = 0;\n1271: \n1272: sock[sockindex] = conn->writesockfd;\n1296:     }\n1297: \n1298:     bitmap |= GETSOCK_WRITESOCK(sockindex);\n1299:   }\n1300: \n1301:   return bitmap;\n1302: }\n1303: \n1304: /* Curl_init_CONNECT() gets called each time the handle switches to CONNECT\n1305:    which means this gets called once for each subsequent redirect etc */\n1306: void Curl_init_CONNECT(struct Curl_easy *data)\n1307: If this\n1701:      * behavior is undesired, the 307 (Temporary Redirect) status code\n1702:      * can be used instead.\n1703:      *\n1704:      * ----\n1705:      *\n1706:      * Many webservers expect this, so these servers often answers to a POST\n1707:      * request with an error page. If this\n1726:      * behavior is undesired, the 307 (Temporary Redirect) status code\n1727:      * can be used instead.\n1728:      *\n1729:      * ----\n1730:      *\n1731:      * Many webservers expect this, so these servers often answers to a POST\n1732:      * request with an error page. To be sure that libcurl gets the page that\n1733:      * most user agents would get, libcurl has to force GET.\n1734:      *\n1735:      * This behavior is forbidden by RFC1945 and the obsolete RFC2616, and\n1736:      * can be overridden with CURLOPT_POSTREDIR.\n1737:      */\n1738:     if((data->state.httpreq == HTTPREQ_POST\n1739:         || data->state.httpreq == HTTPREQ_POST_FORM\n1740:         || data->state.httpreq == HTTPREQ_POST_MIME)\n1741:        && !(data->set.keep_post & CURL_REDIR_POST_302)) {\n1742:       infof(data, \"Switch from POST to GET\");\n1743:       data->state.httpreq = HTTPREQ_GET;\n1744:     }\n1745:     break;\n1746: \n1747:   case 303: /* See Other */\n1748:     /* 'See Other' location is not the resource but a substitute for the\n1749:      * resource. In this case we switch the method to GET/HEAD, unless the\n1750:      * method is POST and the user specified to keep it as POST.\n1751:      * https://github.com/curl/curl/issues/5237#issuecomment-614641049\n1752:      */\n1753:     if(data->state.httpreq != HTTPREQ_GET &&\n1754:        ((data->state.httpreq != HTTPREQ_POST &&\n1755:          data->state.httpreq != HTTPREQ_POST_FORM &&\n1756:          data->state.httpreq != HTTPREQ_POST_MIME) ||\n1757:         !(data->set.keep_post & CURL_REDIR_POST_303))) {\n1758:       data->state.httpreq = HTTPREQ_GET;\n1759:       infof(data, \"Switch to %s\",\n1760:             data->req.no_body?\"HEAD\":\"GET\");\n1761:     }\n1762:     break;\n1763:   case 304: /* Not Modified */\n1764:     /* 304 means we did a conditional request and it was \"Not modified\".\n1765:      * We shouldn't get any Location: header in this response!\n1766:      */\n1767:     break;\n1768:   case 305: /* Use Proxy */\n1769:     /* (quote from RFC2616, section 10.3.6):\n1770:      * \"The requested resource MUST be accessed through the proxy given\n1771:      * by the Location field. The Location field gives the URI of the\n1772:      * proxy.  The recipient is expected to repeat this single request\n1773:      * via the proxy. 305 responses MUST only be generated by origin\n1774:      * servers.\"\n1775:      */\n1776:     break;\n1777:   }\n1778:   Curl_pgrsTime(data, TIMER_REDIRECT);\n1779:   Curl_pgrsResetTransferSizes(data);\n1780: \n1781:   return CURLE_OK;\n1782: #endif /* CURL_DISABLE_HTTP */\n1783: }\n1784: \n1785: /* Returns CURLE_OK *and* sets '*url' if a request retry is wanted.\n1786: \n1787:    NOTE: that the *url is malloc()ed. */\n1788: CURLcode Curl_retry_request(struct Curl_easy *data, char **url)\n1789: {\n1790:   struct connectdata *conn = data->conn;\n1791:   bool retry = FALSE;\n1792:   *url = NULL;\n1793: \n1794:   /* if we're talking upload, we can't do the checks below, unless the protocol\n1795:      is HTTP as when uploading over HTTP we will still get a response */\n1796:   if(data->state.upload &&\n1797:      !(conn->handler->protocol&(PROTO_FAMILY_HTTP|CURLPROTO_RTSP)))\n1798:     return CURLE_OK;\n1799: \n1800:   if((data->req.bytecount + data->req.headerbytecount == 0) &&\n1801:      conn->bits.reuse &&\n1802:      (!data->req.no_body || (conn->handler->protocol & PROTO_FAMILY_HTTP))\n1803: #ifndef CURL_DISABLE_RTSP\n1804:      && (data->set.rtspreq != RTSPREQ_RECEIVE)\n1805: #endif\n1806:     )\n1807:     /* We got no data, we attempted to reuse a connection. For HTTP this\n1808:        can be a retry so we try again regardless if we expected a body.\n1809:        For other protocols we only try again only if we expected a body.\n1810: \n1811:        This might happen if the connection was left alive when we were\n1812:        done using it before, but that was closed when we wanted to read from\n1813:        it again. Bad luck. The Domain Attribute says:\\n140:    * For example, if the value of the Domain attribute is\\n141:    * \\\"example.com\\\", the user agent will include the cookie in the Cookie\\n142:    * header when making HTTP requests to example.com, www.example.com, and\\n143:    * www.corp.example.com.\\n144:    */\\n145:   if(hostname_len == cookie_domain_len)\\n146:     return TRUE;\\n147:   if('.' == *(hostname + hostname_len - cookie_domain_len - 1))\\n148:     return TRUE;\\n149:   return FALSE;\\n150: }\\n151: \\n152: /*\\n153:  * matching cookie path and url path\\n154:  * RFC6265 5.1.4 Paths and Path-Match\\n155:  */\\n156: static bool pathmatch(const char *cookie_path, const char *request_uri)\\n157: {\\n158:   size_t cookie_path_len;\\n159:   size_t uri_path_len;\\n160:   char *uri_path = NULL;\\n161:   char *pos;\\n162:   bool ret = FALSE;\\n163: \\n164:   /* cookie_path must not have last '/' separator. ex: /sample */\\n165:   cookie_path_len = strlen(cookie_path);\\n166:   if(1 == cookie_path_len) {\\n167:     /* cookie_path must be '/' */\\n168:     return TRUE;\\n169:   }\\n170: \\n171:   uri_path = strdup(request_uri);\\n172:   if(!uri_path)\\n173:     return FALSE;\\n174:   pos = strchr(uri_path, '?');\\n175:   if(pos)\\n176:     *pos = 0x0;\\n177: \\n178:   /* #-fragments are already cut off! */\\n179:   if(0 == strlen(uri_path) || uri_path[0] != '/') {\\n180:     strstore(&uri_path, \\\"/\\\", 1);\\n181:     if(!uri_path)\\n182:       return FALSE;\\n183:   }\\n184: \\n185:   /*\\n186:    * here, RFC6265 5.1.4 says\\n187:    *  4. Output the characters of the uri-path from the first character up\\n188:    *     to, but not including, the right-most %x2F (\\\"/\\\").\\n189:    *  but URL path /hoge?fuga=xxx means /hoge/index.cgi?fuga=xxx in some site\\n190:    *  without redirect.\\n191:    *  Ignore this algorithm because /hoge is uri path for this case\\n192:    *  (uri path is not /).\\n193:    */\\n194: \\n195:   uri_path_len = strlen(uri_path);\\n196: \\n197:   if(uri_path_len < cookie_path_len) {\\n198:     ret = FALSE;\\n199:     goto pathmatched;\\n200:   }\\n201: \\n202:   /* not using checkprefix() because matching should be case-sensitive */\\n203:   if(strncmp(cookie_path, uri_path, cookie_path_len)) {\\n204:     ret = FALSE;\\n205:     goto pathmatched;\\n206:   }\\n207: \\n208:   /* The cookie-path and the uri-path are identical. */\\n209:   if(cookie_path_len == uri_path_len) {\\n210:     ret = TRUE;\\n211:     goto pathmatched;\\n212:   }\\n213: \\n214:   /* here, cookie_path_len < uri_path_len */\\n215:   if(uri_path[cookie_path_len] == '/') {\\n216:     ret = TRUE;\\n217:     goto pathmatched;\\n218:   }\\n219: \\n220:   ret = FALSE;\\n221: \\n222: pathmatched:\\n223:   free(uri_path);\\n224:   return ret;\\n225: }\\n226: \\n227: /*\\n228:  * Return the top-level domain, for optimal hashing.\\n229:  */\\n230: static const char *get_top_domain(const char * const domain, size_t *outlen)\\n231: {\\n232:   size_t len = 0;\\n233:   const char *first = NULL, *last;\\n234: \\n235:   if(domain) {\\n236:     len = strlen(domain);\\n237:     last = memrchr(domain, '.', len);\\n238:     if(last) {\\n239:       first = memrchr(domain, '.', (last - domain));\\n240:       if(first)\\n241:         len -= (++first - domain);\\n242:     }\\n243:   }\\n244: \\n245:   if(outlen)\\n246:     *outlen = len;\\n247: \\n248:   return first? first: domain;\\n249: }\\n250: \\n251: /* Avoid C1001, an \\\"internal error\\\" with MSVC14 */\\n252: #if defined(_MSC_VER) && (_MSC_VER == 1900)\\n253: #pragma optimize(\\\"\\\", off)\\n254: #endif\\n255: \\n256: /*\\n257:  * A case-insensitive hash for the cookie domains.\\n258:  */\\n259: static size_t cookie_hash_domain(const char *domain, const size_t len)\\n260: {\\n261:   const char *end = domain + len;\\n262:   size_t h = 5381;\\n263: \\n264:   while(domain < end) {\\n265:     h += h << 5;\\n266:     h ^= Curl_raw_toupper(*domain++);\\n267:   }\\n268: \\n269:   return (h % COOKIE_HASH_SIZE);\\n270: }\\n271: \\n272: #if defined(_MSC_VER) && (_MSC_VER == 1900)\\n273: #pragma optimize(\\\"\\\", on)\\n274: #endif\\n275: \\n276: /*\\n277:  * Hash this domain.\\n278:  */\\n279: static size_t cookiehash(const char * const domain)\\n280: {\\n281:   const char *top;\\n282:   size_t len;\\n283: \\n284:   if(!domain || Curl_host_is_ipnum(domain))\\n285:     return 0;\\n286: \\n287:   top = get_top_domain(domain, &len);\\n288:   return cookie_hash_domain(top, len);\\n289: }\\n290: \\n291: /*\\n292:  * cookie path sanitize\\n293:  */\\n294: static char *sanitize_cookie_path(const char *cookie_path)\\n295: {\\n296:   size_t len;\\n297:   char *new_path = strdup(cookie_path);\\n298:   if(!new_path)\\n299:     return NULL;\\n300: \\n301:   /* some stupid site sends path attribute with '\\\"'. */\\n302:   len = strlen(new_path);\\n303:   if(new_path[0] == '\\\\\\\"') {\\n304:     memmove(new_path, new_path + 1, len);\\n305:     len--;\\n306:   }\\n307:   if(len && (new_path[len - The caller is responsible for checking\\n361:  * for OOM errors.\\n362:  */\\n363: static void strstore(char **str, const char *newstr, size_t len)\\n364: {\\n365:   DEBUGASSERT(newstr);\\n366:   DEBUGASSERT(str);\\n367:   free(*str);\\n368:   *str = Curl_memdup(newstr, len + 1);\\n369:   if(*str)\\n370:     (*str)[len] = 0;\\n371: }\\n372: \\n373: /*\\n374:  * remove_expired\\n375:  *\\n376:  * Remove expired cookies from the hash by inspecting the expires timestamp on\\n377:  * each cookie in the hash, freeing and deleting any where the timestamp is in\\n378:  * the past.  If the cookiejar has recorded the next timestamp at which one or\\n379:  * more cookies expire, then processing will exit early in case this timestamp\\n380:  * is in the future.\\n381:  */\\n382: static void remove_expired(struct CookieInfo *cookies)\\n383: {\\n384:   struct Cookie *co, *nx;\\n385:   curl_off_t now = (curl_off_t)time(NULL);\\n386:   unsigned int i;\\n387: \\n388:   /*\\n389:    * If the earliest expiration timestamp in the jar is in the future we can\\n390:    * skip scanning the whole jar and instead exit early as there won't be any\\n391:    * cookies to evict.  If we need to evict however, reset the next_expiration\\n392:    * counter in order to track the next one. In case the recorded first\\n393:    * expiration is the max offset, then perform the safe fallback of checking\\n394:    * all cookies.\\n395:    */\\n396:   if(now < cookies->next_expiration &&\\n397:       cookies->next_expiration != CURL_OFF_T_MAX)\\n398:     return;\\n399:   else\\n400:     cookies->next_expiration = CURL_OFF_T_MAX;\\n401: \\n402:   for(i = 0; The prime reason for filtering out control bytes is that some HTTP\\n456:   servers return 400 for requests that contain such.\\n457: */\\n458: static int invalid_octets(const char *p)\\n459: {\\n460:   /* Reject all bytes \\\\x01 - \\\\x1f (*except* \\\\x09, TAB) + \\\\x7f */\\n461:   static const char badoctets[] = {\\n462:     \\\"\\\\x01\\\\x02\\\\x03\\\\x04\\\\x05\\\\x06\\\\x07\\\\x08\\\\x0a\\\"\\n463:     \\\"\\\\x0b\\\\x0c\\\\x0d\\\\x0e\\\\x0f\\\\x10\\\\x11\\\\x12\\\\x13\\\\x14\\\"\\n464:     \\\"\\\\x15\\\\x16\\\\x17\\\\x18\\\\x19\\\\x1a\\\\x1b\\\\x1c\\\\x1d\\\\x1e\\\\x1f\\\\x7f\\\"\\n465:   };\\n466:   size_t len;\\n467:   /* scan for all the octets that are *not* in cookie-octet */\\n468:   len = strcspn(p, badoctets);\\n469:   return (p[len] != '\\\\0');\\n470: }\\n471: \\n472: /*\\n473:  * Curl_cookie_add\\n474:  *\\n475:  * Add a single cookie line to the cookie keeping object. The Domain Attribute says:\\n140:    * For example, if the value of the Domain attribute is\\n141:    * \\\"example.com\\\", the user agent will include the cookie in the Cookie\\n142:    * header when making HTTP requests to example.com, www.example.com, and\\n143:    * www.corp.example.com.\\n144:    */\\n145:   if(hostname_len == cookie_domain_len)\\n146:     return TRUE;\\n147:   if('.' == *(hostname + hostname_len - cookie_domain_len - 1))\\n148:     return TRUE;\\n149:   return FALSE;\\n150: }\\n151: \\n152: /*\\n153:  * matching cookie path and url path\\n154:  * RFC6265 5.1.4 Paths and Path-Match\\n155:  */\\n156: static bool pathmatch(const char *cookie_path, const char *request_uri)\\n157: {\\n158:   size_t cookie_path_len;\\n159:   size_t uri_path_len;\\n160:   char *uri_path = NULL;\\n161:   char *pos;\\n162:   bool ret = FALSE;\\n163: \\n164:   /* cookie_path must not have last '/' separator. ex: /sample */\\n165:   cookie_path_len = strlen(cookie_path);\\n166:   if(1 == cookie_path_len) {\\n167:     /* cookie_path must be '/' */\\n168:     return TRUE;\\n169:   }\\n170: \\n171:   uri_path = strdup(request_uri);\\n172:   if(!uri_path)\\n173:     return FALSE;\\n174:   pos = strchr(uri_path, '?');\\n175:   if(pos)\\n176:     *pos = 0x0;\\n177: \\n178:   /* #-fragments are already cut off! */\\n179:   if(0 == strlen(uri_path) || uri_path[0] != '/') {\\n180:     strstore(&uri_path, \\\"/\\\", 1);\\n181:     if(!uri_path)\\n182:       return FALSE;\\n183:   }\\n184: \\n185:   /*\\n186:    * here, RFC6265 5.1.4 says\\n187:    *  4. domain));\\n240:       if(first)\\n241:         len -= (++first - domain);\\n242:     }\\n243:   }\\n244: \\n245:   if(outlen)\\n246:     *outlen = len;\\n247: \\n248:   return first? first: domain;\\n249: }\\n250: \\n251: /* Avoid C1001, an \\\"internal error\\\" with MSVC14 */\\n252: #if defined(_MSC_VER) && (_MSC_VER == 1900)\\n253: #pragma optimize(\\\"\\\", off)\\n254: #endif\\n255: \\n256: /*\\n257:  * A case-insensitive hash for the cookie domains.\\n258:  */\\n259: static size_t cookie_hash_domain(const char *domain, const size_t len)\\n260: {\\n261:   const char *end = domain + len;\\n262:   size_t h = 5381;\\n263: \\n264:   while(domain < end) {\\n265:     h += h << 5;\\n266:     h ^= Curl_raw_toupper(*domain++);\\n267:   }\\n268: \\n269:   return (h % COOKIE_HASH_SIZE);\\n270: }\\n271: \\n272: #if defined(_MSC_VER) && (_MSC_VER == 1900)\\n273: #pragma optimize(\\\"\\\", on)\\n274: #endif\\n275: \\n276: /*\\n277:  * Hash this domain.\\n278:  */\\n279: static size_t cookiehash(const char * const domain)\\n280: {\\n281:   const char *top;\\n282:   size_t len;\\n283: \\n284:   if(!domain || Curl_host_is_ipnum(domain))\\n285:     return 0;\\n286: \\n287:   top = get_top_domain(domain, &len);\\n288:   return cookie_hash_domain(top, len);\\n289: }\\n290: \\n291: /*\\n292:  * cookie path sanitize\\n293:  */\\n294: static char *sanitize_cookie_path(const char *cookie_path)\\n295: {\\n296:   size_t len;\\n297:   char *new_path = strdup(cookie_path);\\n298:   if(!new_path)\\n299:     return NULL;\\n300: \\n301:   /* some stupid site sends path attribute with '\\\"'. */\\n302:   len = strlen(new_path);\\n303:   if(new_path[0] == '\\\\\\\"') {\\n304:     memmove(new_path, new_path + 1, len);\\n305:     len--;\\n306:   }\\n307:   if(len && (new_path[len - 1] == '\\\\\\\"')) {\\n308:     new_path[--len] = 0x0;\\n309:   }\\n310: \\n311:   /* RFC6265 5.2.4 The Path Attribute */\\n312:   if(new_path[0] != '/') {\\n313:     /* Let cookie-path be the default-path. */\\n314:     strstore(&new_path, \\\"/\\\", 1);\\n315:     return new_path;\\n316:   }\\n317: \\n318:   /* convert /hoge/ to /hoge */\\n319:   if(len && new_path[len - The caller is responsible for checking\\n361:  * for OOM errors.\\n362:  */\\n363: static void strstore(char **str, const char *newstr, size_t len)\\n364: {\\n365:   DEBUGASSERT(newstr);\\n366:   DEBUGASSERT(str);\\n367:   free(*str);\\n368:   *str = Curl_memdup(newstr, len + 1);\\n369:   if(*str)\\n370:     (*str)[len] = 0;\\n371: }\\n372: \\n373: /*\\n374:  * remove_expired\\n375:  *\\n376:  * Remove expired cookies from the hash by inspecting the expires timestamp on\\n377:  * each cookie in the hash, freeing and deleting any where the timestamp is in\\n378:  * the past.  If the cookiejar has recorded the next timestamp at which one or\\n379:  * more cookies expire, then processing will exit early in case this timestamp\\n380:  * is in the future.\\n381:  */\\n382: static void remove_expired(struct CookieInfo *cookies)\\n383: {\\n384:   struct Cookie *co, *nx;\\n385:   curl_off_t now = (curl_off_t)time(NULL);\\n386:   unsigned int i;\\n387: \\n388:   /*\\n389:    * If the earliest expiration timestamp in the jar is in the future we can\\n390:    * skip scanning the whole jar and instead exit early as there won't be any\\n391:    * cookies to evict.  If we need to evict however, reset the next_expiration\\n392:    * counter in order to track the next one. In case the recorded first\\n393:    * expiration is the max offset, then perform the safe fallback of checking\\n394:    * all cookies.\\n395:    */\\n396:   if(now < cookies->next_expiration &&\\n397:       cookies->next_expiration != CURL_OFF_T_MAX)\\n398:     return;\\n399:   else\\n400:     cookies->next_expiration = CURL_OFF_T_MAX;\\n401: \\n402:   for(i = 0; i < COOKIE_HASH_SIZE; i++) {\\n403:     struct Cookie *pv = NULL;\\n404:     co = cookies->cookies[i];\\n405:     while(co) {\\n406:       nx = co->next;\\n407:       if(co->expires && co->expires < now) {\\n408:         if(!pv) {\\n409:           cookies->cookies[i] = co->next;\\n410:         }\\n411:         else {\\n412:           pv->next = co->next;\\n413:         }\\n414:         cookies->numcookies--;\\n415:         freecookie(co);\\n416:       }\\n417:       else {\\n418:         /*\\n419:          * If this cookie has an expiration timestamp earlier than what we've\\n420:          * seen so far then record it for the next round of expirations.\\n421:          */\\n422:         if(co->expires && co->expires < cookies->next_expiration)\\n423:           cookies->next_expiration = co->expires;\\n424:         pv = co;\\n425:       }\\n426:       co = nx;\\n427:     }\\n428:   }\\n429: }\\n430: \\n431: /* Make sure domain contains a dot or is localhost. */\\n432: static bool bad_domain(const char *domain, size_t len)\\n433: {\\n434:   if((len == 9) && strncasecompare(domain, \\\"localhost\\\", 9))\\n435:     return FALSE;\\n436:   else {\\n437:     /* there must be a dot present, but that dot must not be a trailing dot */\\n438:     char *dot = memchr(domain, '.', len);\\n439:     if(dot) {\\n440:       size_t i = dot - domain;\\n441:       if((len - i) > 1)\\n442:         /* the dot is not the last byte */\\n443:         return FALSE;\\n444:     }\\n445:   }\\n446:   return TRUE;\\n447: }\\n448: \\n449: /*\\n450:   RFC 6265 section 4.1.1 says a server should accept this range:\\n451: \\n452:   cookie-octet    = %x21 / %x23-2B / %x2D-3A / %x3C-5B / %x5D-7E\\n453: \\n454:   But Firefox and Chrome as of June 2022 accept space, comma and double-quotes\\n455:   fine. The prime reason for filtering out control bytes is that some HTTP\\n456:   servers return 400 for requests that contain such.\\n457: */\\n458: static int invalid_octets(const char *p)\\n459: {\\n460:   /* Reject all bytes \\\\x01 - \\\\x1f (*except* \\\\x09, TAB) + \\\\x7f */\\n461:   static const char badoctets[] = {\\n462:     \\\"\\\\x01\\\\x02\\\\x03\\\\x04\\\\x05\\\\x06\\\\x07\\\\x08\\\\x0a\\\"\\n463:     \\\"\\\\x0b\\\\x0c\\\\x0d\\\\x0e\\\\x0f\\\\x10\\\\x11\\\\x12\\\\x13\\\\x14\\\"\\n464:     \\\"\\\\x15\\\\x16\\\\x17\\\\x18\\\\x19\\\\x1a\\\\x1b\\\\x1c\\\\x1d\\\\x1e\\\\x1f\\\\x7f\\\"\\n465:   };\\n466:   size_t len;\\n467:   /* scan for all the octets that are *not* in cookie-octet */\\n468:   len = strcspn(p, badoctets);\\n469:   return (p[len] != '\\\\0');\\n470: }\\n471: \\n472: /*\\n473:  * Curl_cookie_add\\n474:  *\\n475:  * Add a single cookie line to the cookie keeping object. Let me check if that's possible...\n\nLooking back at line 698, when setting co->domain:\n```c\nstrstore(&co->domain, valuep, vlen);\n```\n\nThe `strstore` function at line 363-371:\n```c\nstatic void strstore(char **str, const char *newstr, size_t len){\n  DEBUGASSERT(newstr);  DEBUGASSERT(str);\n  free(*str);\n  *str = Curl_memdup(newstr, len + 1);\n  if(*str)\n    (*str)[len] = 0;}\n```\n\nSo co->domain will be set to a string. Now, if vlen is 0, then Curl_memdup allocates (0+1) bytes = 1 byte, and then (*str)[0] = 0, so it will be a zero-length string (just a null terminator).\n\nBut at line 669, there's a check:\n```c\nelse if((nlen == 6) &&\n        strncasecompare(\"domain\", namep, 6) && vlen) {\n```\n\nThe `&& vlen` condition ensures that domain values must have non-zero length before being stored, so empty domain strings shouldn't occur.\n\nHowever, there's a fallback mechanism at lines 798-805 where if no domain was parsed from the Set-Cookie header, the function uses a default domain parameter via strdup(domain). This means co->domain ends up either NULL or pointing to an actual string value.\n\nBut I should verify the file parsing path too. Looking at the Netscape cookie file format handling around lines 893-900, when reading from a file, the first field gets assigned directly to co->domain via strdup(ptr). If that first field happens to be empty, then co->domain would point to an empty string instead of NULL.\n\nThe loop condition at line 891 checks `ptr &&`, which ensures ptr isn't NULL, but ptr could still point to an empty string after the leading dot removal. This means strdup(\"\") would successfully allocate memory for an empty string, setting co->domain to that empty string rather than leaving it uninitialized or NULL.\n\nWhen cookie_tailmatch is later called with this empty domain string, strlen(co->domain) returns 0. The function then compares the hostname against itself using strncasecompare with a length of 0, which would match any hostname since comparing zero characters always succeeds. The subsequent checks for hostname_len == cookie_domain_len would also behave unexpectedly when cookie_domain_len is 0, potentially allowing cookies with empty domains to match any host. 0 and cookie_domain_len == 0: it checks if there's a dot at position hostname_len - 1, which would be the last character of the hostname. This means an empty domain would match any hostname ending with a dot, or actually any hostname at all since the dot check becomes meaningless. The core issue is that when cookie_domain_len is 0, the strncasecompare at line 132 compares zero characters and always returns true, allowing an empty domain to match any hostname. This is a critical security flaw because it bypasses domain validation entirely. empty domain should not match any hostname. The fix would be to add a check at the beginning of cookie_tailmatch to return FALSE if cookie_domain_len is 0.\n\nI've identified a defect: the cookie_tailmatch function in lib/cookie.c (lines 123-150) fails to handle empty cookie domains properly. When cookie_domain_len is 0, the code attempts to access hostname[hostname_len - 1] without validation, which could cause incorrect matching behavior or buffer underflow. The function should reject empty domains outright rather than attempting domain matching
